## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate expressed as a function of time t and population size P, which is the standard setup for continuous-time population dynamics in ecology. Typical structures encode per-capita growth (1/P * dP_dt) with density dependence, carrying capacity, Allee effects, harvesting, and time-varying environmental forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Exponential with time-varying rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (linear trend in environment affecting per-capita growth)
- Exponential with periodic forcing: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (seasonal variation in growth rate)
- Quadratic density dependence (Verhulst form in derivative): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (crowding/competition reduces growth)
- General polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = P * (c0 + c1 * P + c2 * P**2) (per-capita growth as polynomial in density)
- Gompertz growth (ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (log-linear decline of per-capita growth with P)
- Richards / generalized logistic (ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P**c2) (flexible curvature via exponent c2)
- Theta-logistic (alternative parameterization): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**(c2 + 1) (density dependence exponent controls approach to carrying capacity)
- Allee effect (strong Allee, cubic): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (negative growth at low P, positive at intermediate P)
- Allee effect (smooth rational per-capita term): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) / (P + c2) (facultative/strong Allee with saturation at high P)
- Harvesting (constant yield): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 (removal independent of P)
- Harvesting (proportional): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P (mortality/harvest proportional to P)
- Harvesting with saturation (Holling type II removal): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P / (c3 + P) (limited harvest/predation capacity)
- Von Bertalanffy-type growth (in size-like P): dP_dt = c0 * P**(c1) - c2 * P (anabolic vs catabolic scaling; c1 often < 1)
- Environment-modulated carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (effective carrying capacity changes exponentially with time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth analysis: rewrite as (dP_dt)/P = f(t, P); if f decreases with P, expect density dependence; if f is constant in P, expect density-independent growth.
- Carrying-capacity behavior: terms like -c * P**2 or (1 - c * P**a) create a stable equilibrium where dP_dt crosses zero at finite P.
- Superlinear negative density dependence: exponents P**(a+1) with a>1 imply very strong crowding (steeper slowdown near high P) compared to quadratic.
- Allee signatures: factors (P - c) or (P - c)/(P + c) create negative growth below a threshold population, implying extinction risk at low P.
- Harvest/mortality separation: additive negative terms (-c, -c*P, -c*P/(c+P)) indicate external removal; their functional form suggests constant, proportional, or capacity-limited removal.
- Seasonality/nonstationarity: coefficients that depend on t (e.g., c0 + c1*sin(c*t)) indicate periodic resource/weather forcing and can generate cycles even without explicit predator variables.
- Log-type feedback: log(c*P) in dP_dt suggests multiplicative effects where per-capita growth declines approximately linearly with log-population (Gompertz-like).
- Near-zero behavior: if dP_dt has leading factor P, then P=0 is an equilibrium; if dP_dt includes -c (constant harvest), extinction can occur in finite time once P is small.
- Scaling/heterogeneity clues: fractional powers P**c (0<c<1) often indicate surface/transport-limited or allometric growth constraints rather than pure crowding.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (BPG1)
============================================================
GT: c0*P*exp(-c1*t) + c2*P**c3/(c4*P + c5)
Candidate formulas: 50

GT is the fixed function
\[
f(t,P)=A\,P e^{-kt} \;+\; A\,\frac{P^2}{B P+1}
\]
with \(A=0.3156057016002752\), \(k=0.05405074842498068\), \(B=9.870854086995406\).

So any matching candidate must be exactly “(linear in \(P\))·exp(-kt)” plus a **time-independent** rational term equal to \(A P^2/(BP+1)\). In particular:
- The only \(t\)-dependence in GT is \(e^{-kt}\) multiplying **exactly \(P\)** (not \(P^2\), not \((P^2+P)\), not divided by \(P+\text{const}\)).
- The rational term is \( \propto \frac{P^2}{BP+1}\) with denominator linear in \(P\) and constant term \(1\), and it has **no \(t\)**.

Now check candidates.

1. Has several terms with common denominator \(P+c1\) and also \(exp(c4 t)\) inside that fraction, plus an extra \(exp(c7 t)\cos(c8 t)\). To match GT, all non-GT functional forms must vanish: set \(c6=0\). But remaining \(t\)-dependent part is \(\frac{P^2 c3 e^{c4 t}+P c5 e^{c4 t}}{P+c1}=e^{c4 t}\frac{P(P c3+c5)}{P+c1}\), which cannot equal \(A P e^{-kt}\) for all \(P\) unless the fraction is constant in \(P\). That would require \(P(Pc3+c5)\propto (P+c1)\), impossible (LHS is degree 2 unless \(c3=0\), then degree 1 but still \(P c5\) cannot be proportional to \(P+c1\) for all \(P\) unless \(c1=0\) and then it becomes constant \(c5\), giving \(c5 e^{c4 t}\) (no \(P\)). So no.

2. Same structural issue as (1) plus sinusoid term \(P c6\sin(\cdot)\) (must set \(c6=0\)). Still cannot produce \(P e^{-kt}\) term. No.

3. Extra \(c6\cos(c7\exp(c8|t|))\) must be 0; remaining same issue: \(t\)-dependence trapped in \((P+c1)^{-1}\) with \(P^2\) and \(P\) mixture. Cannot equal \(P e^{-kt}\). No.

4. Extra \(c6 e^{c7 t}\) must be 0; remaining same issue. No.

5. Extra \(c6 t (P+c7)^{c8}\) must be 0; remaining same issue. No.

6. Extra \(c6 \exp(P^{c7}c8)\) must be 0; remaining same issue. No.

7. Extra polynomial terms \(P c6 + P^{c7}c8\) must be 0 (set \(c6=0\) and \(c8=0\)). Remaining same issue. No.

8. Has term \(P*P^{c5}c6 = c6 P^{c5+1}\) and \(P c8\); must be 0. Still has \(t\)-dependent fraction with wrong \(P\)-structure. No.

9. Extra \(P^{c6}c7 e^{c8 t}\) must be 0; remaining same issue. No.

10. Contains a standalone \(P^2 c2\) and \(P c7\) (must be 0), but still \(t\)-dependent part is \(\frac{P^2 c4 e^{c5 t}+P c6 e^{c5 t}}{P+c1}\) which cannot become \(A P e^{-kt}\). No.

11. Has polynomial \(P^3 c0 + P^2 c1\) (must be 0), leaving \(\frac{P^2 c4 e^{c5 t}+P c6 e^{c5 t}+P^2 c2}{P+c3}\). Same obstruction: \(t\)-dependent part divided by \(P+c3\). No.

12. Many extra polynomial terms \(P^3 c0, P^2 c3, P^2 c4, P c8\) etc. Even if zeroed, \(t\)-dependent part remains divided by \(P+c2\). Cannot yield \(P e^{-kt}\). No.

13. Extra \(c6 e^{P c7}\) must be 0; remaining same issue. No.

14. Has \(P c5 (c6+t)^{c7}\) which must be 0; remaining still has \(t\)-dependent fraction issue. No.

15. Has \(P c5/(c6 t+c7)\) and \(c9/(c6 t+c7)\); must be 0. Remaining still has \(t\)-dependent fraction issue. No.

16. Extra \(P^{c6}c7\) must be 0; remaining same issue. No.

17. Form: \(P^2 c0 + \frac{P^2 c1}{P+c2} + \frac{P^2 c3 e^{c4 t}}{P+c2} + \frac{P c5 e^{c4 t}}{P+c2}\).
To match GT, the \(t\)-dependent part must be \(A P e^{-kt}\) with no \(P\)-denominator. Here it is \(e^{c4 t}\frac{P(P c3+c5)}{P+c2}\), same impossibility as above. No.

18. Extra \(c6 t^{c7}\) must be 0; remaining same issue. No.

19. Extra \(P c6 t\) must be 0; remaining same issue. No.

20. Extra \(P c6 \log(P c7+1)\) must be 0; remaining same issue. No.

21. Extra sinusoid term must be 0; remaining same issue. No.

22. Extra affine in \(t\) term \(c6 t+c7\) must be 0; remaining same issue. No.

23. Extra rational-in-\(t\) terms must be 0; remaining same issue. No.

24. Has additional terms \(P^2 c5 e^{c4 t}+P c6 e^{c4 t}\) **not** over \(P+c1\). Even if set \(c5=c6=0\), remaining is the same problematic fraction. If not set to 0, then \(t\)-dependent part includes \(P^2 e^{c4 t}\) which GT does not have. No.

25. Adds extra rational-in-\(P\) term \(P^2 c5/(P+c6)+P c7/(P+c6)\) (time-independent) which could be zeroed, but still cannot fix the \(t\)-dependent fraction problem. No.

26. Adds \(P c5/(P c6+c7)+c9/(P c6+c7)\) which must be 0; still same issue. No.

27. Adds \(t\)-dependent terms with denominator \(P c7+c8\) which must be 0; still same issue. No.

28. Extra \(c6\log(c7 t+1)\) must be 0; still same issue. No.

29. Extra sinusoid in \(t\) must be 0; still same issue. No.

30. Structure: \(P^{1/3}c0 + \frac{P\cdot P^{c1}c2}{P^{c1}+c3} + P c4 + P c5 + P c6 e^{c7 t}\).
To match GT, need exactly one exponential term \(A P e^{-kt}\): set \(c6=A\), \(c7=-k\), and set \(c0=0,c4=0,c5=0\). Then need \(\frac{P^{c1+1}c2}{P^{c1}+c3}=A\frac{P^2}{BP+1}\).
Choose \(c1=1\) to get \(\frac{P^2 c2}{P+c3}\). Then set \(c3=1/B\) and \(c2=A/B\):
\[
\frac{P^2 (A/B)}{P+1/B}=\frac{A P^2}{B P+1}
\]
Exactly GT. So candidate 30 can match.

**GT:** `0.3156*P*exp(-0.0541*t) + 0.3156*P²/(9.871*P + 1)`

Let me rewrite GT in a more general symbolic form:
`c0*P*exp(-c1*t) + c2*P²/(c4*P + c5)`

The key structural components are:
1. A term `P*exp(-c1*t)` — exponential decay in t, linear in P
2. A term `P²/(c4*P + c5)` — rational function of P only

Let me analyze the common structure shared by many candidates. Many candidates have the form:

`P²*c0/(P+c1) + P²*c2/(P+c1) + P²*c3*exp(c4*t)/(P+c1) + P*c5*exp(c4*t)/(P+c1) + [extra terms]`

Let me simplify the common part. Combining over denominator (P+c1):
`[(c0+c2)*P² + c3*P²*exp(c4*t) + c5*P*exp(c4*t)] / (P+c1)`
= `[P²(c0+c2) + P*exp(c4*t)*(c3*P + c5)] / (P+c1)`

For this to match GT, I need:
- The rational part: `(c0+c2)*P²/(P+c1)` should give `c_GT*P²/(c_GT*P + 1)` — this works by choosing c1 appropriately and scaling.
- The exponential part: `P*exp(c4*t)*(c3*P + c5)/(P+c1)` should give `a*P*exp(b*t)`

For the exponential part to equal `a*P*exp(b*t)`, we need `(c3*P + c5)/(P+c1)` to be a constant. This requires c3/1 = c5/c1, i.e., c5 = c3*c1. Then `(c3*P + c3*c1)/(P+c1) = c3`. So the exponential part becomes `c3*P*exp(c4*t)`.

This works! So the "base" structure (candidates 38, etc.) with these 4 terms over (P+c1) CAN match GT.

Now let me check each candidate. The base structure (Candidates with exactly these terms and nothing else, or with extra terms that can be zeroed):

The rational (non-exponential) part is `c0*P²/(P+c1)` which matches the GT rational part. The exponential part is `P*exp(c3*t)*(c2*P+c4)/(P+c1)` which needs `(c2*P+c4)/(P+c1)` to be constant, requiring c2 = c4/c1. Then it becomes `c2*P*exp(c3*t)`. This MATCHES.
